25:T2922,<entryFree id="n40939" key="هِجْرَةٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">هِجْرَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, a subst. from <foreign lang="ar">هَجَرَهُ</foreign>, (S, K,) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40939-1" target="هِجْرَانٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40941"/></foreign>, (Msb,) signifying The <hi rend="ital">cutting another off from friendly</hi> or <hi rend="ital">loving communion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">intercourse:</hi> (S:) <hi rend="ital">cutting one;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ceasing to speak to him:</hi> (K:) <hi rend="ital">forsaking, abandoning, deserting,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">shunning</hi> or <hi rend="ital">avoiding, one.</hi> (Msb.) It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">لَا هِجْرَةَ بَعْدَ ثَلَاثٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There shall be no cutting off from friendly communion after three</hi> nights with their days,]: the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">هَجْرٌ</foreign> as contr. of <foreign lang="ar">وَصْلٌ</foreign>; i. e., such anger as exists between Muslims, or a failing, or falling short, with respect to the duties of society, exclusively of what relates to religion: but the <foreign lang="ar">هِجْرَة</foreign> of those who follow their own natural desires [in matters of religion], and of innovators [in religion], should continue even as long as they do not repent, and return to the truth. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Also, <hi rend="ital">A mode,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">manner, of cutting another off from friendly</hi> or <hi rend="ital">loving communion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">intercourse:</hi> &amp;c. See 1, where an ex. occurs.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also, <hi rend="ital">A removal from the desert to the towns</hi> or <hi rend="ital">villages:</hi> this was its [primary] acceptation with the Arabs: and the <hi rend="ital">forsaking of his country,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">district,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, by an inhabitant of the desert,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by an inhabitant of a town,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">village,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cultivated district, and taking up his abode in another country</hi> or <hi rend="ital">district,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, an emigration;</hi> (TA;) the <hi rend="ital">forsaking of one's home and removing to another place;</hi> (Mgh;) the <hi rend="ital">forsaking of a country,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">district,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, and removing to another;</hi> (Msb;) the <hi rend="ital">going forth from one land to another;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40939-2" target="هُجْرَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40938"/></foreign>. (K:) [and <hi rend="ital">an emigration from the territory of the unbelievers to the territory of the believers,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to any place of safety</hi> or <hi rend="ital">refuge on account of religious persecution &amp;c.:</hi> see 3, last signification:] a subst. from <foreign lang="ar">هَاجَرَ</foreign>. (Msb, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">الهِجْرَةٌ</foreign>, peculiarly, <hi rend="ital">The emigration,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">flight,</hi> (for it was really a flight,) of Mohammad, from Mekkeh to Yethrib, which latter was afterwards called El-Medeeneh. Hence, <foreign lang="ar">تَأْرِيخُ الهِجْرَةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The era of the Hijreh,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Flight.</hi> The epoch of this era is not the date of the Flight itself, as some have imagined, (for this took place on an uncertain day, most probably the first or second, of the third lunar month of the Arabian year,) but is the first day of the Arabian year in which the Flight happened: and as I believe that all European writers who have attempted to fix it, prior to M. Caussin de Perceval, have erred respecting it, the true date, as shown by him, (see his “ Essai sur l'Histoire des Arabes, ” &amp;c., in the places referred to in the index to that <pb n="2881"/> work,) I think it important here to mention. The first year of the Flight was the two hundred and eleventh year of a period during which the Arabs made use of a defective luni-solar reckoning, making every third year to consist of thirteen lunar months; the others consisting of twelve such months. This mode of reckoning was abolished by Mohammad in the twelfth month of the tenth year of the Flight, at the time of the pilgrimage; whence it appears that the first year of the Flight commenced, most probably, on Monday, the nineteenth of April, A. D. 622; or perhaps on the eighteenth; for the actual appearance of the new moon properly marked its commencement, and, as the new moon happened about sunset on the sixteenth, it may perhaps have been seen on the eve of the eighteenth. According to M. Caussin de Perceval, the first ten years of the Flight commenced at the following periods. <Table>

                  </Table> Thus it appears that the first and fourth and seventh years were of thirteen lunar months each; and the seventh was the last year that was thus augmented: therefore, with the eighth year commenced the reckoning by common lunar years; and from this point we may use the tables which have often been published for finding the periods of commencement of years of the Flight. We must not, however, rely upon the exact accuracy of these tables: for the commencement of the month was generally determined by actual observation of the new moon; not by calculation; and we often find that a year was commenced, according as the place of observation was low or high, or to the east or west of the place to which the calculation is adapted, or according as the sky was obscure or clear, a day later or earlier than that which is indicated in the tables; and in some cases, even two days later. The twelfth day of the third month of the first year of the Flight, the day of Mohammad's arrival at Kubà, was Monday: therefore the first day of the year was most probably the nineteenth of April, as two months of thirty days each, or twenty-nine days each, seldom occur together. But the tenth day of the first month of the sixty-first year, the day on which El-Hoseyn was slain at Kerbelà, was Friday: therefore the first day of that year, at that place, must have been Wednesday, the third of October, A. D. 680; not the first of October, as in most of the published tables above mentioned. (For the principal divisions of the Arabian year when the luni-solar reckoning was instituted, see <foreign lang="ar">زَمَنٌ</foreign>)]. <foreign lang="ar">الهِجْرَتَانِ</foreign> means [<hi rend="ital">The two emigrations,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">flights;</hi> namely,] <hi rend="ital">the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">هِجْرَة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">to Abyssinia and the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">هِجْرَة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">to El-Medeeneh.</hi> (S, K.) And <foreign lang="ar">ذُو الهِجْرَتَيْنِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (of the <foreign lang="ar">صَحَابَة</foreign> [or Companions of Mohammad] TA) <hi rend="ital">who emigrated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">who has emigrated, to Abyssinia and to El-Medeeneh.</hi> (K.)    </entryFree>26:T1d7e,<entryFree id="n40929" key="هَجَرَهُ" type="main">

                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">هَجَرَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, A, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">

                  </form>, (Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">هَجْرٌ</foreign> (S, A, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">هِجْرَانٌ</foreign>, (S, A, Mgh, K,) or the latter is a simple subst., (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He cut him off from friendly</hi> or <hi rend="ital">loving, communion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">intercourse; contr. of</hi>

(A.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">صَلَاةُ <ref cref="n40948-4" target="الهَجِيرِ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The prayer of noon;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">الهَجِيرُ</foreign>, elliptically. (TA.) See also <foreign lang="ar">ظَهِيرَةٌ</foreign>.    </entryFree>2f:T60b,<entryFree id="n40954" key="مَهْجُورٌ" type="main">

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مَهْجُورٌ</orth>

                  <hi rend="ital">Cut off from friendly</hi> or <hi rend="ital">loving communion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">intercourse; forsaken,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abandoned: cut,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">not spoken to.</hi> (Mgh, Msb.) In like manner <foreign lang="ar">مَهْجُورًا</foreign> is used in the Kur, [xxv. 32,] signifying <hi rend="ital">avoided,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forsaken, with the tongue,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with the heart</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mind.</hi> (B.) [But see what here follows.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  Talk, or language, <hi rend="ital">uttered irrationally</hi> or <hi rend="ital">foolishly</hi> or <hi rend="ital">deliriously.</hi> It is related by Aboo-'Obeyd, on the authority of Ibráheem, that the words of the Kur, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ قَوْمِى ٱتَّخَذُوا هٰذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱلْقُرْآنَ مَهْجُورًا</foreign>, [xxv. 32,] mean, <hi rend="ital">Verily my people have made this Kur-án a thing of which they have said what is not true:</hi> because the sick man, when he talks irrationally or foolishly or deliriously, says what is not true: and the like is related on the authority of Mujáhid.
